# live-spec Roadmap (dated version: 2026-07-18 — updated at every edit; SPEC M-3)

The wish queue. Intake is continuous — a wish lands here the moment it is spoken. Execution is serial:
the current landing finishes before the next starts. Class = size (bug / small / surface / large — one
vocabulary with the spec) plus a priority mark when it isn't normal: a critical bug lands before
everything; a quick win may bubble up between landings, the jump marked in its row (SPEC T-11, INV-12).
A row also names its DOOR — feature · bug · refactor · docs-only · skip — said at intake, before any
code; feature tripwires outrank a casual label and queue-cutting stays with the bug door (SPEC T-12, INV-16).
And it names its WORK-KIND — product · infra · skill · prose — what the wish builds; the kind scales the
form each pipeline step takes, and a stood-down step is named in the landing report, never silently
skipped (SPEC T-16, INV-22).

Closed rows live in dated archives under docs/queue-archive/ (INV-1); this table holds the ACTIVE queue.

| 334 | **A test-cleanup kill must never match the human's real browser** (tlvphotos inbox incident 2026-07-15 ~20:36, `inbox/2026-07-15-from-tlvphotos-test-cleanup-killed-users-real-chrome.md`) — **HIGH, safety, reaches outside git**: clearing stray test browsers between flaky runs, the agent and briefed workers used over-broad kill patterns — `pkill -9 -f "chrome_crashpad_handler"`, `pkill -9 chrome`, "pkill Chrome before each run" — which match the USER'S real Google Chrome (`chrome_crashpad_handler` is the user's own Chrome's process; bare `chrome` matches "Google Chrome"). Alexander's browser closed mid-session, destroying his own work state — an irreversible outward effect [base rule 17] the row-222 hygiene law and the harness law mean to forbid. The pack's canonical harness itself is safe (it reaps only its OWN process group via `start_new_session` + prefers Chrome for Testing under `~/.cache/puppeteer`), but the MANUAL/worker cleanup around a flaky run has NO stated safety rule, so it defaulted to broad name patterns; and a worker briefed "pkill chrome" reinvents the footgun. Fix — state the GENERAL law, not a chrome blocklist (Alexander 2026-07-15: this isn't only about the browser, it applies to any shared resource; check who is currently using it, if that's knowable): **a cleanup removes or kills only what THIS run provably created and owns, and never a SHARED resource in current use by another party** (the human, another live process, another session). The class is any shared resource — a process, a temp dir, a port, a file, a lock, the display — the browser is one instance. The operational test is current use: before touching a shared resource, where ownership/use is KNOWABLE (a live PID, a recorded owner marker, an install path, a lock file, an open handle) it MUST be checked, and a resource in use or of unprovable ownership is left untouched. This UNIFIES today's three incidents into one law — the browser (in use by the human), orphan processes (330/331, already: never reap a live owner-pid), the temp dir (333, already: sweep only dead/old, never a live sibling's dir); the harness already embodies it for its own resources via owner-pid liveness, so the law lifts that outward. Concrete for the browser: the only legal kill target is the test browser uniquely (its `~/.cache/puppeteer/...` install path or the harness's own recorded PID / process group); the forbidden broad patterns (bare `chrome` / `Chrome` / `Google Chrome` / `chrome_crashpad_handler` / bare `puppeteer`) can match the human's real browser and are banned. Prefer NO manual kill at all (the harness's own-group reap + install-path sweep removes the need; a manual pkill is the scoped fallback only). Homes: the harness law (INV-157/158 family) + the worker-briefing guidance + base rule 17 (irreversible outward effects). Mechanical net: a guardrail greps briefs/scripts for a forbidden broad kill pattern and reds. | small | **landed 2026-07-15 (v1.10.0); door: feature (INV-162) + docs (worker-briefing); kind: skill; footprint: cross-cutting.** INV-162 states the general own-and-not-in-use law; the guardrail `check-broad-kill.sh` reds a bare-name browser kill in a tracked script (`.sh`/`.py`/`.js`/`.ts`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`), wired into the push gate (CI gate j + local pre-push) and the worker-briefing guidance. The MINOR-gate prover found the LAW sound but the first-cut NET weak — it caught the exact incident but five evasions slipped (a path in a comment laundering a kill, `killall`/`kill $(pgrep)`/pipe-to-kill, unscanned `.js`, the delete half unnetted, and an over-claimed "greps a brief"); all folded — comments stripped before the scope check, the verb set widened to `pkill`/`killall`/`kill`, JS/TS globs added, the three nets named to what each covers (guardrail for the kill, owner-liveness sweep + temp-diff for the delete, prose for the brief), and the owned-lineage case (a prior run's provably-dead owner [INV-157]) added; record `docs/prover/2026-07-15-334-cleanup-ownership.md`. Red-proven; every evasion is now a regression test. | 391 | **Every net keeps its own liveness numbers, and a silent net is read rather than trusted** (the owner's word, 2026-07-17: he hopes later models will not need these hooks, and he asked for something that monitors them and takes a hook away when it stops firing; born of the same hour's finding that the pack's Stop-event scan had run a handful of times across a three-hour session and read one message per run, so every violation between tool calls passed untouched): a net that never fires is a fact about itself, and the fact has two readings — the defect is gone and the net is dead weight to retire, or the net is broken and its trigger sits where the work does not pass. Two numbers tell them apart, and no net keeps them today: how often it RAN and how often it FIRED. | 396 | **Two agents on one machine talk directly; git carries what needs no answer** (the owner's word, 2026-07-17, refusing the transport premise this stage was built on: agents will not talk through git, that is dumb — there should be direct protocols between agents on one machine, certainly on one machine; git carries the requests that need no particular reply, and notifications): the premise came from the seed and I built INV-183 on it — a remote seat reaches a repo through git alone [INV-112], therefore git is the universal transport and co-location is only a fast path. That reasons from the worst case to the general rule, and his split cuts by the TRAFFIC's kind instead: a thing needing no timely answer takes the durable, auditable, slow road (a file, a commit); a conversation takes a direct channel. The channel law survives untouched — INV-183 is about WHO talks and WHEN, and one sentence inside it about transport is what needs correcting. **The fact nobody has checked: whether two Claude Code sessions on one machine have a direct channel at all.** They are independent processes and may have none by default; a socket, a watched file, or a harness mechanism may exist. That is verified, never derived — check it before designing. This also re-reads the 2026-07-17 research (docs/research/): its closing line was that no prior art fits a repo-as-unit, git-as-transport setting; drop the git premise and the question becomes what direct agent-to-agent protocols exist, which is a different sweep. | 395 | **An expensive architectural decision earns a stated way to be decided, and agent birth is its first member** (the owner's word, 2026-07-17, continuing the multi-agent thread: if the pack ever decides to create a new agent, that decision must be very well thought through — with Fable, adversarially AND directly, or some other smart way; it is an expensive architectural decision, and that CLASS of decisions needs a strong grounding. He asks whether the class has other members. He named a reference he had heard of, unverified by us: a Karpathy skill for this kind of decision-making, one advocate and one prosecutor among several, deciding together): three parts. (a) NAME THE CLASS — what makes a decision expensive is that unwinding it costs more than making it: a new agent (a tree, a queue, a gate set, a registry seat, a standing mission, and every consumer's pin), a node carve or merge [INV-113, INV-122], a contract's shape once a consumer pins it [INV-187], a project's kind [INV-36], a public repo going public. | 438 | **A prover lens for delivery separability along a declared composition axis** (Alexander via the tlvphotos window, 2026-07-21 inbox wish, his catch mid the input-modality-axis movement): composition asks whether BEHAVIOUR splits along a declared cross-cutting axis; the dual asks whether the delivered ARTIFACT splits along that same axis or ships as one monolith. The prover forces the design to state "this axis ships monolithically because X" or "this axis owes a platform-split / lazy-load road", and the absence of that statement is the finding.
